<div id="review_1661410930" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1661410930" />
    <a title="Kostas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas"><img alt="Kostas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554812738p2/25638423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1661410930?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kostas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kostas" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas">Kostas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780099683018" href="/book/show/553145.City_of_Golden_Shadow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=cyberpunk">cyberpunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=science-fantasy">science-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1661410930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6125800033343648654">8.5/10<br/><br/>This is the second series that I’m reading from Tad Williams and I have to say that I’m really impressed of how different it is compared to his most famous series, <i>Memory, Sorrow and Thorn</i>, although personally I quite liked it even if it’s not outstanding.<br/>In this series Tad Williams changes his style and goes to Science Fiction but he also raises his skill level as he has mixed Cyberpunk, lots of mystery and a touch of Fantasy that, I believe, makes all the difference!<br/><br/>The story is set most</span>
  <span id="freeText6125800033343648654" style="display:none">8.5/10<br /><br />This is the second series that I’m reading from Tad Williams and I have to say that I’m really impressed of how different it is compared to his most famous series, <i>Memory, Sorrow and Thorn</i>, although personally I quite liked it even if it’s not outstanding.<br />In this series Tad Williams changes his style and goes to Science Fiction but he also raises his skill level as he has mixed Cyberpunk, lots of mystery and a touch of Fantasy that, I believe, makes all the difference!<br /><br />The story is set mostly in Africa, in a world far more technologically advanced than our own, where people are now using Virtual Reality for everything; even more than their actual life, doing whatever they want without limitations. But when a group of kids accidentally fall onto something that they weren’t supposed to discover, a secret that no one knows, they will find themselves against an evil that does not even hesitate to kill in order to protect it.<br />However Renie, an instructor in virtual engineering at a polytechnic institution, having seen her brother fall victim to this evil, she will try with her friend !Xabbu, one of the last hunters of the ancient tribe of the Bushman, to find what was this secret and who was chasing him so she can save him.<br />On the other hand, Ronald, a kid from America has also seen something unexpected and he will also begin his own quest for the truth, while Paul, a soldier from the WW1, who no longer remembers who he was before will travel to unknown worlds and see things that didn’t believe were possible.<br />Their paths will not be easy and the secrets will only multiply as they go on but all the answers seem to be in the golden city, Otherland; a city that has actually more secrets than they know and their enemy that is chasing them is, perhaps, even worse.<br /><br />For a first book in this huge series I must say that is actually quite good even though Williams’ familiar problem with the size of his stories, but he has made, once again, a very rich world and with incredible ideas.<br />His witting is really easy but flows quite good without tiring as much as his others books and the characters are all well drawn and interesting enough as we discover their secrets and of their world; only Christabel, I would say, didn’t hold me much but she has rather small role in the story so I can’t say it really bothered me.<br />My biggest complain would be for the ending, which is really abrupt, but Williams explains (in the next book) that the series is one story, one “book”, just split in four parts.<br /><br />In general, Williams might not have fast paced stories or flashy action scenes as other writers but his world-building and the mystery of the hidden city are, for me, what I think really stand out in this book and are, indeed, that which kept reading till the end. He’s not perfect but he definitely shines, in his own way, so if you like his style, even a little, give this a try.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6125800033343648654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_151017930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151017930" />
    <a title="Aleah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3398219-aleah"><img alt="Aleah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436270185p2/3398219.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151017930?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aleah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aleah" href="/user/show/3398219-aleah">Aleah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3398219-aleah?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151017930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6165883017240090530">In the first installment of Tad Williams "Otherworld" series the reader is introduced to a future where the net and virtual reality are readily available to anyone with enough credits. A virtual reality professor at a South African University, Renie Sulaweyo, becomes good friends with her student, !Xabbu, one of the last remaining African Bushmen. Renie and !Xabbu become entangled in a conspiracy involving the most powerful and dangerous men in the world. The scope of what needs to be done is mo</span>
  <span id="freeText6165883017240090530" style="display:none">In the first installment of Tad Williams "Otherworld" series the reader is introduced to a future where the net and virtual reality are readily available to anyone with enough credits. A virtual reality professor at a South African University, Renie Sulaweyo, becomes good friends with her student, !Xabbu, one of the last remaining African Bushmen. Renie and !Xabbu become entangled in a conspiracy involving the most powerful and dangerous men in the world. The scope of what needs to be done is more than Renie can really comprehend, but she can't give up while her young brother, Stephen, is somehow entangled in these powerful men's dark machinations.<br /><br />I continue to be surprised by how prophetic Science Fiction can seem. "City of Golden Shadow" was published in 1996, but in it Williams imagines people watching "netflicks" instead of movies. His young characters spend hours battling monsters with their online friends, a nod to the popularity and evolution of massively multiplayer online roleplaying games (MMORPGs). (After some cursory checking* it seems the company Netflix didn't begin operations until a year later, in 1997, the same year that the acronym MMORPG came into use.) <br /><br />Suffice it to say that this novel gave me everything that I love about Tad Williams -- an intricate plot, detailed world building and enough details to choke a horse. Williams weaves the sci-fi elements of networked computing and virtual reality with traditional South African folklore, to beautiful effect. A strong female lead character was just icing on this yummy sci-fi cake. <br /><br />* I looked it up Wikipedia. Don't judge.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6165883017240090530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1836968537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8080821952735168109">I started out reading the hardcover, which had been gifted me and really did want to finish reading it, but was having difficult because I couldn’t carry it around with me. After 2.5 years I was about ready to give up, when the audiobook was finally released. It still took me 6 months to listen to it. <br/><br/>The novel is made up of 4 or 5, maybe more, individual stories, which seem to have nothing to do with one another. It isn’t until about half way through this brick when ever so tenuously bits of st</span>
  <span id="freeText8080821952735168109" style="display:none">I started out reading the hardcover, which had been gifted me and really did want to finish reading it, but was having difficult because I couldn’t carry it around with me. After 2.5 years I was about ready to give up, when the audiobook was finally released. It still took me 6 months to listen to it. <br /><br />The novel is made up of 4 or 5, maybe more, individual stories, which seem to have nothing to do with one another. It isn’t until about half way through this brick when ever so tenuously bits of stories would find a link. Of course, from there it was a bit of a cascade where the threads became more and more interwoven and finally end up coming together in the last few chapters. Now of course, I have to continue with the series, because nothing got resolved! I’m really curious about where this all is going.<br /><br />The narrator was really good, using well-done accents to delineate characters. Unfortunately there was not enough space between scene changes and I found myself confused and having to go back. A longer silence or even a little sound to signal the end of one scene and the beginning of the next would’ve been helpful. </span>

<div id="review_76629572" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76629572" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2689336-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251769542p2/2689336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76629572?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/2689336-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2689336-ashley?shelf=never-finished">never-finished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76629572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13256317815732067145">This novel, to me, is 780 pages of nothing. With five main characters, there is a lot of running around, random descriptions that seem to me are pretty uneccessary, and a LOT of confusion. When a new chapter starts, there is a tendency of character switching, so you are left with a few pages just trying to figure out which character you are focusing on. If Williams only focused on Renie and !Xabbu, I would have been content with this novel, considering that's where most of the focus is on, anywa</span>
  <span id="freeText13256317815732067145" style="display:none">This novel, to me, is 780 pages of nothing. With five main characters, there is a lot of running around, random descriptions that seem to me are pretty uneccessary, and a LOT of confusion. When a new chapter starts, there is a tendency of character switching, so you are left with a few pages just trying to figure out which character you are focusing on. If Williams only focused on Renie and !Xabbu, I would have been content with this novel, considering that's where most of the focus is on, anyways.<br /><br />Pros: When the story actually focus' on a single character and continues with the plot, it is actually pretty entertaining.<br /><br />Cons: Random breaks, no cliff-hanger chapter endings, unneccessary detail, random POV (point-of-view) character switching... the list can go on.<br /><br />Judgement: I personally couldn't muster up the will to finish this novel. I got through about half of it until I said "Enough is enough... I need something better to read." I'll probably save this for winter or summer break, when I absolutely have NOTHING better to do.<br /><br />Meh, it was less than okay. 2/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13256317815732067145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222135443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7176221602827065633">Really enjoyed this, lots of different worlds and good characters. No resolution at the end though, will just have to get the second book in the series to find out what happens next.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lanica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lanica" href="/user/show/1336787-lanica">Lanica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=series-complete">series-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27474429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8359548111988828547">I read the Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn series and loved it. I read it twice and have autographed copies to save. I enjoy epics. I enjoy detail. I enjoy science fiction, computers, virtual reality, anthropology, history, sociology, political intrigue and all the other individual elements of this series. Unfortunetly, I really disliked this book.<br/><br/>I liked the little girl who got messages through her computer, and I liked the sick boy who created a virtual reality that was easier to live in. Other than</span>
  <span id="freeText8359548111988828547" style="display:none">I read the Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn series and loved it. I read it twice and have autographed copies to save. I enjoy epics. I enjoy detail. I enjoy science fiction, computers, virtual reality, anthropology, history, sociology, political intrigue and all the other individual elements of this series. Unfortunetly, I really disliked this book.<br /><br />I liked the little girl who got messages through her computer, and I liked the sick boy who created a virtual reality that was easier to live in. Other than those two I could care less about any of the characters, and there were a lot of characters. I read the whole book thinking that there should be some sort of connection between them, but it didn't come. I waited for the plot to advance, yet it seemed to seep slowly through the pages and pages of detail. <br /><br />I read the second book and found that some of these ideas came together, but not quickly or interestingly enough to hold my attention. I didn't read book three or four and don't intend to. This was a great dissapointment to me. I have to really dislike a book to set it aside, and that it was a series from one of my favorite authors was really heartbreaking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8359548111988828547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1071653247" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1071653247?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Ryan" href="/user/show/7151669-anthony-ryan">Anthony Ryan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1071653247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13580004349215571781">Williams' near-future sci-fi epic is a compelling exploration of the social/psychological costs and benefits posed by the advent of true virtual reality. A disparate cast of heroes find themselves trapped in an array of artificially constructed realities where death is an all too real possibility. Williams' pedigree as an epic fantasy author is evident in the scope of the narrative and the presence of a dark lord of sorts lurking at the heart of this web of invented worlds. Reading the whole ser</span>
  <span id="freeText13580004349215571781" style="display:none">Williams' near-future sci-fi epic is a compelling exploration of the social/psychological costs and benefits posed by the advent of true virtual reality. A disparate cast of heroes find themselves trapped in an array of artificially constructed realities where death is an all too real possibility. Williams' pedigree as an epic fantasy author is evident in the scope of the narrative and the presence of a dark lord of sorts lurking at the heart of this web of invented worlds. Reading the whole series is a big commitment but I found it well worth the investment.</span>

<div id="review_476424813" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/476424813" />
    <a title="Christopher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7077333-christopher"><img alt="Christopher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493712208p2/7077333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/476424813?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christopher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christopher" href="/user/show/7077333-christopher">Christopher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12806720-city-of-golden-shadow">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer476424813&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer476424813" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11531435191938734203">City of Golden Shadow is the first book in the Otherland series and is a look at a future, though fairly near future, world where the internet has continued to evolve into a VR network that people use to go about their daily tasks and for entertainment! :D The title Otherland refers to a quasi secret part of these virtual worlds that has been put in place by a rich grouping of people known as the Grail Brotherhood and it is around this that some of the story revolves as our main characters come </span>
  <span id="freeText11531435191938734203" style="display:none">City of Golden Shadow is the first book in the Otherland series and is a look at a future, though fairly near future, world where the internet has continued to evolve into a VR network that people use to go about their daily tasks and for entertainment! :D The title Otherland refers to a quasi secret part of these virtual worlds that has been put in place by a rich grouping of people known as the Grail Brotherhood and it is around this that some of the story revolves as our main characters come together and our plunged into these hyper realistic simulations that once they are in they find that they cannot leave! :D<br /><br />The stories main characters come from all walks of life and places ranging from South Africa To the America's, London and the rest of the world but through the VR network they eventually meet and form a team who are questing by the end of the book in what ironically could be called an adventuring considering that everyone is wearing a VR model of themselves which does add a subtle extra bit of tongue in cheek humour to events that are taking place! :D<br /><br />Initially because of the wide separation of the characters and in differences in scenarios our main characters and the emerging plotlines appear to have nothing in common with each other but as the story progresses more and more of the plotlines start to merge and the overall plot starts to emerge with various events and characters filling in the gaps though through example of Renie as she investigates while so many children are ending up in unexplainable coma's after going online! :D <br /><br />This all gives the book a big sense of adventure while at the same time we get many mysteries involved as well which also gives the sense of mystery while our characters try and find out what is happening while trying to some power hungry virtual Egyptians! :D<br /><br />City of Golden Shadow forms and lays out a very large canvass for the other books and shows us a future world that in many way we have the technological base for now and gives us a view of what this evolving technology will mean for us! :D At the same time amongst all the conspiracies we get to see vast vista's which change from one moment another and back again in the VL world! :D At the same time you get to see that these virtual worlds can be used for good as well which helps to keep the events of the books in context for the characters! :D There are also the moral sides of things with Renie not being sure about whether the simulation puppets are alive and for who is actually a good person or not depending on your point of view and raises a host more questions that this level of technology will invariable eventually ask with all its unlimited uses! :D<br /><br />City of Golden Shadow is a vast book that clearly sets up things for the next one but always coming up with new mysteries to be explored and not any real answers but done in a way that the characters all come across as intelligent though but still preserving a lot of the mystery though there are a host more questions raised once a certain city is found! :D Many of the mysteries will not be solved to you have ready the net ones! :D<br /><br />Brilliant and highly recommended! :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="11531435191938734203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120317505" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4253367-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120317505?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/4253367-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120317505" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6272839571834979803">(Whole story - All four volumes)This is, without a doubt, the best series novel I have ever read. Multiple plot lines in a fantastic world that slowly twist and turn until they eventually merge. A simple beginning, children falling into comas for no apparent reason, leads to an epic quest typical of fantasy but applied to science fiction, the historical novel, Victorian children's literature, detective fiction, myth and much, much more. A large cast of unforgettable characters, written beautiful</span>
  <span id="freeText6272839571834979803" style="display:none">(Whole story - All four volumes)This is, without a doubt, the best series novel I have ever read. Multiple plot lines in a fantastic world that slowly twist and turn until they eventually merge. A simple beginning, children falling into comas for no apparent reason, leads to an epic quest typical of fantasy but applied to science fiction, the historical novel, Victorian children's literature, detective fiction, myth and much, much more. A large cast of unforgettable characters, written beautifully by Tad Williams, produce one of those stories that leave you empty and a little pissed off once it has finished. No more being moved to tears in some places, driven to tension headaches in others, being left breathless with wonder in many. If there was ever a story that should receive the cinematic LOTR treatment then this is it but I cannot help but think it wou;ld be a colossal disappointment, would Hollywood welcome two of the main characters - a black South African woman and her Kalahari Bushman student/friend with his apposite knowledge of Bushman myth?<br />Thisd must be the biggest novel I have ever read and love it so much, I try to get everyone I talk to about books to read it. It is just so good!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6272839571834979803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14954945802793598295">The Matrix has them and they can't escape. If you die in the Matrix do you die in real life? They don't know yet and they don't want to find out. I haven't read The Neuromancer, but I assume this book was greatly influenced by it. I was hooked right from the beginning though some of the middle was quite repetitive at times with the "what could be happening....who could be behind this" questions but still a page turner. You're left hanging at the end so it's another "a bit to thick and heavy to r</span>
  <span id="freeText14954945802793598295" style="display:none">The Matrix has them and they can't escape. If you die in the Matrix do you die in real life? They don't know yet and they don't want to find out. I haven't read The Neuromancer, but I assume this book was greatly influenced by it. I was hooked right from the beginning though some of the middle was quite repetitive at times with the "what could be happening....who could be behind this" questions but still a page turner. You're left hanging at the end so it's another "a bit to thick and heavy to read in bed" book to deal with. Almost a five star. Looking forward to the next book in the series.</span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YoNRiudLpiNR7JLD55sAra7GjPSa6xWkpJ8R0eh28Wy3xthBI3gUjUaJyx7u6YruuvBW21x9olW2MtepAWSa1g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('p5pD8Xglc6RaVHfY5VElanjsQSPgz39/IFKcwHfXlKdy38o6vBbBCk0xLgXsI68pbNqbDCZZyI4y/1q4nsX/HQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Lo<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText45981469794381667\" style=\"display:none\">Waking up in a strange house, with no memory of how or why he is there, Stuart Milton finds his life has changed beyond recognition. His pregnant wife is missing, but his only living relative, his brother, is incapable of substantiating his claim. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15704774247475036926">Tad Williams is a California-based fantasy superstar. His genre-creating (and genre-busting) books have sold tens of millions worldwide, in twenty-five languages. His considerable output of epic fantasy and science fiction book-series, stories of all kinds, urban fantasy novels, comics, scripts, etc., have strongly influenced a generation of writers: the ‘Otherland’ epic relaunches June 2018 as an</span>
  <span id="freeText15704774247475036926" style="display:none">Tad Williams is a California-based fantasy superstar. His genre-creating (and genre-busting) books have sold tens of millions worldwide, in twenty-five languages. His considerable output of epic fantasy and science fiction book-series, stories of all kinds, urban fantasy novels, comics, scripts, etc., have strongly influenced a generation of writers: the ‘Otherland’ epic relaunches June 2018 as an MMO on steam.com. Tad is currently immersed in the creation of ‘The Last King of Osten Ard’, planned as a trilogy with two intermediary novels. He, his family and his animals live in the Santa Cruz mountains in a suitably strange and beautiful house. @tadwilliams @mrstad</span>
